================================ Paragraph 212 =================================

Until two years ago, interaction with speech scientists had been minimal since the end of the DARPA  Speech Understanding Program in 1976. Progress ha natural language processing should contribute directly to  spoken language systems. This is true not only where understanding seems to be necessary, e.g.-, voice commands  and requests, translation of speech, etc., but also in speech transcription. The error rate of speech recognition  systems is directly correlated with the perplexity of the language to be recognized. Statistical language models in  speech transcription have given the lowest perplexity thus far, and therefore, the best performance. Language  processing techniques, whether supplemental or in place of current statistical models, offer the potential of providing  even lower perplexity due to modeling both local and global constraints, as well as supporting speech applications  other than transcription.
